тАШ рдЖ рдпрд╛рддреНрд╡рд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдореЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореИрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН ред тАШрдЖ рдпрд╛рддреБ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН ред рдкреГрд╖реНрдареНрдпрд╛рднрд┐рдкреНрд▓рд╡рд╖рдбрд╣рдпреЛрдГ рдкреНрд░рдердореЗрд╜рд╣рдиреНрдпреЗрддрдиреНрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдиреАрдпрдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ- рдЖ рдпрд╛рддреНрд╡рд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░реЛрд╜рд╡рд╕ рдЗрддрд┐ рдорд░реБрддреНрд╡рддреАрдпрдореН’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рен.рел.резрео) рдЗрддрд┐ редред

Jamison Brereton

21 (317)
Indra
V─Бmadeva Gautama
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The first verses of this hymn, especially 1 and 3, are quite reminiscent of the open ing of the preceding hymn, IV.20, with the invitation to Indra to come to our sac rifice from wherever he might be, and the hymn promises to be a straightforward celebration of IndraтАЩs presence at the sacrifice and our praise and offering to him, in the hopes of his goods and help. But the hymn veers off into a different, and deeply puzzling, direction. The pivot is verse 5, which begins with a relative clause as does verse 4, leading us to expect that the referent in verse 5 will be the same as in verse 4, namely Indra, the subject of our hymn. But it is not, as the last word reveals, but rather the Hotar, here almost certainly the god Agni.
The next three verses (6тАУ8) share a number of features: repeated phrases (espe cially the go╠Бhe phrase of 6b, 7c, 8c), metrical irregularity in their odd p─Бdas (6c, 7a, 7c), morphological and syntactic parallelism, and patterns of phonological and morphosyntactic repetition. But what they especially share is almost impenetrable obscurity. In our admittedly speculative interpretation, these verses take off from the Agni verse (5) and treat simultaneously the kindling of the ritual fire, which initiates the sacrifice here and now, and the Vala myth. As we noted in the introduc tion to IV.20, the twin of this hymn in some ways, the Vala myth, is a backgrounded model for IndraтАЩs generous giving in that hymn. It should also be remembered that the Agni hymns of this maс╣Зс╕Нala frequently take the Vala myth as their subject (see esp. IV.1 and 2), despite the fact that Agni is not usually a participant in that myth. Thus a condensed version of the Vala myth embedded in an Indra hymn but focus ing on Agni is compatible with the larger concerns of the V─Бmadeva poets.
In verse 6 the gods coming to the sacrifice seem to be compared to the Aс╣Еgirases going to the Vala caveтАФthough neither group is mentioned by nameтАФand the seat of both groups is identified as the тАЬsecret placeтАЭ (go╠Бha) of the Au┼Ыija, a vr╠еddhi derivative that we interpret as referring to the whole company of U┼Ыij-priests, or fire-priests. In the second half of the verse the ritual fire is kindled, though with difficulty. The kindled fire roars to life in verse 7a, enabling the sacrifice to proceed (p─Бda b) and the cows in the Vala cave to go forth (p─Бdas cd)тАФexpressed in increas ingly compressed phraseology. The final verse of this section (8) is the one that most clearly alludes to the opening of the Vala cave, using several of the signature words of that myth, including the verb vid├бt тАЬfound, finds,тАЭ which several times in the Vala myth takes тАЬcowsтАЭ as object (I.62.3, V.45.8, X.68.11). But in our verse the object is omitted, presumably to allow the simultaneous reading тАЬcowsтАЭ (for the Vala myth) and тАЬgoodsтАЭ (for the ritual here-and-now).
Having thus provided Indra with a mythic model for generous giving (however cryptically phrased), the poet then reproaches Indra in verse 9 for not participating in the sacrificial give-and-take. The poet ends the hymn with a more conventional summary verse and plea for goods and help (vs. 10), followed by the V─Бmadeva Indra-cycle refrain (vs. 11).

Jamison Brereton Notes

рд╕рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН рдЕрд╡рд╕реЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рдЙрдк рдЖ рдпрд╛рддреБ рдЙрдкрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ ред рдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЗрд╣ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ ред рд╢реВрд░рдГ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рд╡рд╡реГрдзрд╛рдирдГ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзреЛрд╜рдпрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╕рдзрдорд╛рджрд╕реНрддреБ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рдорд╛рджреНрдпрдиреН рднрд╡рддреБ ред рдпрд╕реНрдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рддрд╡рд┐рд╖реАрдГ рддрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпреЛ рдмрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реАрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реНрдпреЛ рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐ ред рд╕рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рдпрд╢реНрдЪреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рджреНрдпреМрд░реНрди рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрд╡ рдЕрднрд┐рднреВрддрд┐ рдкрд░рдХреАрдпрдВ рдмрд▓рдорднрд┐рднрд╛рд╡реБрдХрдВ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрдВ рдмрд▓рдВ рддреЗрдЬреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдкреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рддреН рдкреБрд╖реНрдпрддреБ ред рд╕ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдЙрдкрд╛рдпрд╛рддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрдг рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra come to us for protection, and being praised (by us), may the mighty hero be exhilarated along with (us) at this rite; he whose energies are many; may he, like the radiant sun, recruit his own overpowering vigour.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 20.47; along with us: vasa, with the gods, devai saha; or, asm─Бbhiс╕е saha; lie the radiant sun: dyaur na kс╣гс╣нram abhibh┼лti puс╣гyati, whose many exploits (are celebrated) like the heaven;

Kс╣гatram = may he, (Indra) cherish (our) strength.

Jamison Brereton

Let Indra drive here, near to us, for help. Praised, let the champion be here as our feasting companion,
he whose powers are many when he has grown strong, (whose)
overwhelming dominion, like heaven, will thrive.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published translation, this vs. bears some resemblance to the first vs. of the preceding hymn: our first p─Бda ─Б╠Бy─Бtu ├нndr├│ тАШvasa ├║pa naс╕е more or less lexically matches IV.20.1ab ─Б╠Бna ├нndro тАж ├бvase y─Бsat. See also vs. 3 below.

The second hemistich is syntactically problematic; see OldenbergтАЩs extensive n. The problem is that both nom. sg. v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn├бс╕е and the gen. sg. rel. prn. y├бsya appear to refer to Indra. Geldner interprets y├бsya as a reflexive rel. (see n. 1c): тАЬder erstarkt seine vielen Kr├дfte,тАЭ but not only am I not aware of other reflexive uses of the relative, but this tr. requires that the med. participle v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn├б- be transitive, which it is usually not (though, to be fair, a reflexive transitive would probably require middle voice).

Although the published translation is syntactically trickier (by cutting the p─Бda into two syntactic pieces), it avoids both problems by taking the participle as a separate clause (тАЬwhen he has grown strongтАЭ) and the antecedent to y├бsya in a rel. clause that begins with t├бviс╣г─лс╕е. In this interpr. t├бviс╣г─лс╕е тАж p┼лrv─л╠Бс╕е is nom., not acc. The relative also has domain over the clause in d, with y├бsya limiting kс╣гatr├бm, which is taken as a nom., not acc. as in most tr. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬwie der Himmel seine ├╝berlegene Herrschaft entfalten m├╢geтАЭ also violates the standard construction of similes, by making the simile clausal, with the verb p├║с╣гy─Бt in the simile seeming to correspond to the participle v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn├бс╕е in the frame. (Witzel Got┼НтАЩs tr. of d avoids this problem; their rendering is quite similar to the published translation)

Griffith

MAY Indra come to us for our protection; here be the Hero, praised, our feast-companion.
May he whose powers are many, waxen mighty, cherish, like Dyaus, his own supreme dominion.

Geldner

Indra soll zu uns zum Beistand kommen, hier soll der gepriesene Held Zechgenosse sein, der erstarkt seine vielen Kr├дfte wie der Himmel seine ├╝berlegene Herrschaft entfalten m├╢ge.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorify the powerful leaders of that renowned and opulent (Indra), whose victorious and protecting energy rules over men, like a universal sovereign entitled to veneration.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The powerful leaders: vс╣Ыс╣гny─Бni nс╣Ыn = balabh┼лt─Бn netс╣Ыn, i.e., the Maruts

Jamison Brereton

Here will you praise the bullish forces of him alone, the powerfully brilliant and powerfully generous man,
whose resolve, conquering and victorious like a sovereign king making ceremonial distributions, overwhelms the separate peoples.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn in p─Бda b is problematic. It appears to be an acc. pl., and in fact is an acc. in the same phrase tuvir─Б╠Бdhaso nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn in V.58.2 (referring to the Maruts). But here the undoubted gen. sg. tuvidyumn├бsya immediately preceding (and morphologically parallel to tuvir─Б╠Бdhasaс╕е) invites a gen. sg. reading also of ambiguous tuvir─Б╠Бdhasaс╕е. This in turn presents us with several choices: 1) to take nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn as a real gen. sg., 2) to assume that the last two words were borrowed from V.58.2 (or based on the formula found therein) and not adjusted morphologically, so that nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn is functionally a gen. sg. but formally an acc. pl., or 3) to detach nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn syntactically from what precedes it. Oldenberg opts for option 2 (see disc. in ZDMG 55 [1901]: 745-47 = KlSch. 286-88). He assumes that since tuvir─Б╠Бdhasaс╕е can represent either acc. pl. or gen. sg., when the formula in V.58.2 was imported here, nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn could come along for the ride, functioning as a gen. sg. though adopted from an acc. pl. environment. The third tack is taken by Geldner, who takes с╣Зс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn as a complement of gen. sg. tuvir─Б╠Бdhasaс╕е (тАЬdes тАж gegen die M├дnner FreigebigenтАЭ), and by Witzel Got┼Н, somewhat differently. The latter take nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn as a second obj. of stavatha (besides vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зy─Бni), with the two genitives preceding it hanging off it and modifying Indra: тАЬтАж seine stierhaften (Kr├дfte) sollt ihr hier preisen, (und) die M├дnner des тАжтАЭ (A fourth option, a variant of 3, would be possible: to take tuvir─Б╠Бdhaso nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn as the 2nd acc. obj., with only tuvidyumn├бsya a gen.) Presumably the тАЬmenтАЭ Witzel Got┼Н have in mind are the Maruts, who do appear with Indra in the very next vs. (mar├║tv─Бn 3c) and as just noted are the referents of the undoubted acc. phrase in V.58.2. As for option 1, without endorsing this solution I would point out that a variant of this might be possible. The expected gen. sg. to the root noun

*nс╣Ы╠Б-, based on comparison with Aves. n╟Эr╟Э┼б, should be monosyllabic *n├║r (like pit├║r) (see AiG III.212), *nuс╕е in pausa. Clearly this brief and opaque form didnтАЩt stand much of a chance of preservation as such; but I wonder if, esp. in formulaic phrases like tuvir─Б╠Бdhaso *n├║с╕е, it wasnтАЩt substituted for by the acc. pl. nс╣Ы╠Б╠Дn, the only other (surviving) monosyllabic form in the paradigm, whose affiliation to nс╣Ы╠Б- was much clearer.

In d the verb abhy ├бsti тАШoverwhelmsтАЩ picks up the nominal abh├нbh┼лti- тАШoverwhelming(ness)тАЩ in 1d, with the substitution of тИЪas for тИЪbh┼л.

Griffith

Here magnify his great heroic exploits, most glorious One, enriching men with bounties,
Whose will is like a Sovran in assembly, who rules the people, Conqueror, all-surpassing.

Geldner

Seine Bullenkr├дfte sollet ihr hier preisen, des Glanzreichen, gegen die M├дnner Freigebigen, dessen Umsicht wie ein weiser K├╢nig ├╝berlegen, aus Not helfend, die V├╢lker beherrscht.

Grassmann

Ihr preiset hier ja seine Heldenkr├дfte, die Mannen auch des Gut- und Glanz-erf├╝llten, Dess Macht hervorragt, wie im Rath der K├╢nig, vordringend siegreich ├╝ber alle V├╢lker.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra, accompanied by the Maruts come quickly for our protection, from the heaven, from the earth, from the firmament, or from the waters; from the sphere of the sun, from (any) distant region, from the abode of the rains.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let Indra along with the Maruts drive here from heaven or from the earth, swiftly from the sea or from fertile ground,
from the realm of solar glory, or from afar, from the seat of truth, to help us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this vs. also recalls the opening vs. of the preceding hymn. There the verb ─Б╠БтАж y─Бsat тАШhe will drive hereтАЩ is construed with two ablatives of place-from-which (near and far), plus ├бvase тАШfor helpтАЩ + naс╕е. Here ─Б╠Бy─Бtu, also with ├бvase naс╕е, is construed with no fewer than six ablatives of the same type, elaborating on the near/far contrast to provide a universe of choices.

On p├║r─лс╣гa- see comm. ad I.163.1.

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take sv├аrс╣Зara- as a PN, but this interpr. does not fit the pattern of the vs., and moreover sv├аrс╣Зara- as PN seems to be confined to Maс╣Зс╕Нala VIII. See Mayrhofer (PN, s.v.), who also sees the name only in VIII.

Griffith

Hither let Indra come from earth or heaven, hither with speech from firmament or ocean;
With Maruts, from the realm of light to aid us, or from a distance, from the seat of Order.

Geldner

Indra soll alsbald vom Himmel, von der Erde kommen, vom Meere oder vom Urquell, von Svarnara, uns zum Beistand in Begleitung des Marut, oder aus der Ferne von dem Sitz des Gesetzes.

Grassmann

Es komme Indra her von Erd’ und Himmel, vom Meer hereilend oder von dem Dunstraum, Vom Sonnengott zu H├╝lf’ uns mit den Maruts, von Ferne oder von der Opferst├дtte.

Elizarenkova

рдпрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╕реНрдереВрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрдереВрд▓рд╕реНрдп рдмреГрд╣рддрдГ рдорд╣рддрдГ рд░рд╛рдпрдГ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рдИрд╢реЗ рдИрд╖реНрдЯреЗ рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗрд╖реБ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗрд╖реБ ред рд╡рд┐рджрде рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рддрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН рдЙ’ рддрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдореЗрд╡ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╕реНрддрд╡рд╛рдо ред рдпрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдирд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд░реВрдкреЗрдг рдмрд▓реЗрди рдЧреЛрдорддреАрд╖реБ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рд╕реБ рдЬрдпрддрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпрддреЗ ред рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреБрдпрд╛ рдзреГрд╖реНрдгреБрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЧрд▓реНрднреЛ рдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдиреН рд╡рд╕реНрдпрдГ рд╡рд╕реАрдпрдГ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардВ рдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдзрдирдореН рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ рдЕрднрд┐ рдкреНрд░ рдирдпрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ ред рддрдореЗрд╡реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рд╕реНрддрд╡рд╛рдореЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрдг рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe glorify, in solemn rites, this Indra who rules over substantial, abundant riches; who by his prowess is victor over (hostile) hosts; who by his munificence brings excellent (wealth) to the presence (of his worshippers).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who is master of substantial, lofty wealth, him will we praise at the ceremonial distributionsтАФIndra,
who is the winner along with V─Бyu when (refreshments) consisting of cows are at stake and who boldly leads (us) forth to a better state.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes g├│mat─лс╣гu as referring to a particular river basin and Witzel Got┼Н to тАЬcowrich (rivers)тАЭ – the latter apparently flg. GrassmannтАЩs тАЬrinderreicher Ort.тАЭ But the mention of IndraтАЩs companion V─Бyu here points to a ritual, not battlefield, victory, specifically the morning pressing when Indra and V─Бyu receive the first oblations. There are two nouns that are regularly modified by g├│mati- in the fem. pl.: тАШdawnsтАЩ (uс╣г─Б╠Бsaс╕е) and тАШrefreshmentsтАЩ (├нс╣гaс╕е). Either of them would work in this context. The published translation

supplies the latter, functioning as a loc. absol.: тАЬwhen (refreshments) consisting of cows [that is, milk and butter] are at stake.тАЭ ├нс╣г- does not have an attested loc. pl., and if it did, it would not be pretty or easily recognized: *ikс╣г├║? iс╣нс╣г├║? It would therefore not be surprising if such a form were gapped, with the final of the adj. (-─лс╣гu) gesturing towards it phonologically. However, it is also possible that тАЬat the cow-rich dawnsтАЭ is meant, given that the ritual in question happens at that time. uс╣г├бs- also lacks an attested loc. pl., though we should probably expect *uс╣г├бtsu (see my 1991 тАЬOx, Cart,тАЭ 90-91). Again, gapping this awkward form would not be surprising.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet the invoking priest bring to our dwellings that (Indra) who, firmly fixing the (world) returns food for (sacrificial food), and (utters) a voice enjoining (men) to worship; he who is to be propitiated by praises, who is adored by many.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Utters a voice enjoining men to worship: v─Бcam janayam yajudhyai = the speech of Indra is the thunder

Jamison Brereton

Whoever, piling reverence upon reverence, rouses speech, begetting it in order to perform the sacrifice,
aiming straight, granting many favors, he should bring Indra here to the (ritual) seats with his hymnsтАФhe, the Hotar [=Agni?].

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take с╣Ы├▒jas─Бn├б- to be built to the anomalous 1st sg. middle с╣Ы├▒jase (for which see comm. ad IV.8.1), pace Jasanoff 2016 (etc.), based in part on the shared constr.

с╣Ы├▒jas- GOD (acc.) HYMN (instr.) exemplified, e.g., by IV.8.1 y├бjiс╣гс╣нham с╣Ы├▒jase gir─Б╠БтАЬI aim towards the best sacrificer with a songтАЭ (cf. VI.15.1) and our с╣Ы├▒jas─Бn├бс╕е тАж ukth├бiс╕е тАж ├нndram тАЬaiming straight at Indra with hymns.тАЭ (In fact I would now favor slightly changing the text of the published translation to тАЬaiming straight with his hymnsтАЭ rather than translating uktha├нс╕е with the following p─Бda as in the published translation) The creation and maintenance of the stem с╣Ы├▒jas─Бn├б- is supported by the other -as─Бn├б- secondary participles, on which see comm. ad IV.3.6.

Griffith

May the Priest, Lord of many blessings, striving,-who fixing reverence on reverence, giving
Vent to his voice, inciteth men to worshipwith lauds bring Indra hither to our dwellings.

Geldner

Der Huldigung auf Huldigung t├╝rmt, die Rede treibt, sie hervorbringend, um zu opfern, der vielbegehrte Hotri, der den Vortritt hat, soll mit seinen Lobgedichten den Indra zu den Opfersitzen herbringen.

Grassmann

Der an Verehrung eng Verehrung schliessend, die Stimm’ erhebt, zum Opferdienst ermunternd, Der gabenreiche Priester, vorw├дrts strebend, durch Spr├╝che schaff er her zum Sitz den Indra.

Elizarenkova

рдзрд┐рд╖рдгреНрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рдзрд┐рд╖рдгрд╛рдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ рдФрд╢рд┐рдЬрд╕реНрдп ред рдЙрд╢рд┐рдЬрдГ рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГред рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреНрдпреМрд╢рд┐рдЬреЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдп рдЧреЛрд╣реЗ рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рд╕рджрдиреНрддрдГ рдирд┐рд╖реАрджрдиреНрддреЛ рдЬрдирд╛рдГ рдЕрджреНрд░рд┐рдореН ред рдЖрджреГрдгрд╛рддрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЗрддреНрдпрджреНрд░рд┐рд░рд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ ред рддрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рдзрд┐рд╖рд╛ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛ рдпрджрд┐ рдпрджрд╛ рд╕рд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдЙрдкрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдпреБрдГ рддрджрд╛ рд╕ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЖ рдпрд╛рддреБ ред рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рдВрд╡рд░рдгреЗрд╖реБ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рд╖реБ рдирд┐рд░реЛрдзреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд╣реНрдирд┐рдГ рд╡реЛрдврд╛ рдкрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╕реНрддреНрдпреЗ рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рд╡рд╕рддрд╛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЗрди рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддрд╛ рджреБрд░реЛрд╖рд╛рдГ рджреБрд╕реНрддрд░рдХреНрд░реЛрдзрдГ рдпрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рднреВрддреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рд╕ рдЖрдпрд╛рддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the repeaters of (his) commendations, abiding in the dwelling of the worshipper, approach Indra with praise, may he who is our (great) sustainer in conflicts, whose wrath is difficult to be (appeased), becomes the ministering priest of the master of the house.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Of the worshipper: au┼Ыijasya, from u┼Ыij, a priest, one who employs priests;

Indra: adri is the name in the text, a name, it is said, of Indra, from dri to divide, to tear, as foes

Jamison Brereton

When they [=the gods/Aс╣Еgirases?], seeking a holy place, will hasten to the rock with holy fervor, taking their seats at the secret place of (the company of) the fire-priests [=ritual ground/Vala cave?],
the Hotar [=Agni] of (the company) belonging to the household, (though) he is hard to kindle, (comes into being) hereтАФhe who is the great draft-horse for us in the (ritual) enclosures.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the introduction, I think vs. 6 simultaneously depicts the godsтАЩ approach to the ritual ground and the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ journey to the Vala cave. The rock (├бdri-) to which they hasten is the pressing stone in the case of the gods and the Vala cave in the case of the Aс╣Еgirases.

In p─Бda a I interpret y├бdi as y├бd *─л, parallel to y├бd ─лm in 7a and 7c and y├бd(#)─л in 8d. For this phenomenon, see my 2002 “RVic s─лm and ─лm.тАЭ With Geldner I take ├бdrim as the goal of saraс╣Зy─Б╠Бn rather than construing it with s├бdantaс╕е, allowing the latter participle to be construed with the loc. g├│he (a stem found only here, in the three vss.

6-8).

For dhiс╣г─Б╠Бsee comm. ad I.173.8 as well as I.3.2. The denom. dhiс╣гaс╣Зy├б- is found only here; I take it as тАШseeking a holy placeтАЩ, derived from dhiс╣г├бс╣З─Б тАШholy placeтАЩ, on which see comm. ad I.3.2.

Note the phonetic echoes in dhiс╣г─Б╠Бya(di) dhiс╣гaс╣Зy├бn(taс╕е) (sar)aс╣Зy─Б╠Бn.

As indicated in the published introduction. I take au┼Ыij├б-, the vс╣Ыddhi deriv. of u┼Ы├нj- тАШpriest, fire priestтАЩ, as referring to the collectivity of these priests (see also V.41.5). It seems to be parallel to / contrastive with the vс╣Ыddhi deriv. in the next p─Бda, p─Бsty├б-, found only here, тАШbelonging to the dwelling placeтАЩ. In my interpr. the dur├│с╣г─Бс╕е h├│t─Б is Agni, and p─Бsty├б- refers to the collectivity that he belongs to or represents, that of the household.

On the problematic dur├│с╣г─Бс╕е (here apparently an -s-stem, as opposed to the thematic stem found in the two other occurrences), see comm. ad VIII.1.13.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As discussed in the published introduction, the next few vss. are very challenging; they have received multiple interpretations, which canтАЩt be discussed in detail here.

The vss. form a unity based on their shared vocab. (e.g., g├│he 6b, 7c, 8c; au┼Ыij├бsya 6b, 7c), their shared syntactic formulae (y├бd *─л 6a, y├бd ─лm 7a, 7c, and y├бd ─л 8d), and their shared metrical irregularity.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTrue it is that this might of the son of the protector of the world, the showerer (of benefits), affects for his advantage the offerer of praise; it (prevails) in the secret (thoughts) of the worshipper, and in his dwelling, for (the accomplishment of his) pious acts, (the attainment of his) desires, and his delight.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The protector of the world: bh─Бrvara = patronymic of Bh─Бrvara, which means jagadbhart─Б, the protector of the world, or, Praj─Бpati; in the secret thoughts: the text has guh─Б pra; this is expanded into: guh─Бr┼лpa hс╣Ыdaye prabhavati, the strength,balam, of Indra, prevails or presides over the heart, in the nature of secrecy or mystery; the purport of the entire verse is that the might of Indra always protects his worshipper, Indrasya balam sarvad─Б vajam─Бnam p─Бlayati

Jamison Brereton

When in its entirety the explosive force of the devouring bull [=Agni] accompanies him [=Agni?], for the praiser to take his reward,
when (it accompanies) him secretly to the secret place of (the company of) the fire-priests, when (it accompanies him) in order (for the
praiser) to go forth to insight, forth to exhilarationтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another very opaque vs. The only thing we have to hold onto is structure: the X-─Б y├бd ─лm of p─Бdas a and c recalls X-─Б╠Бy├бd *─л of 6a, and notice X y├бd dhi(y├й) in p─Бda d. The whole vs. is a subordinate clause (or series of them), continued by 8ab, with the main clause in 8c – and a final y├бd(#)─л clause rounding out the sequence in 8d.

As indicated in the published translation, I think vs. 7 depicts the bursting into flames of the ritual fire, whose difficult kindling was (possibly) treated in 6cd. This bursting into flames is expressed by ┼Ы├║с╣гmaс╕е тАШexplosive forceтАЩ in 7b. The gen. bh─Бrvar├бsya vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зaс╕е тАШdevouring bullтАЩ refers to Agni, in this interpr.; the only two forms to the (pseudo-)root тИЪbharv тАШdevourтАЩ have Agni as their subj. (I.143.5, VI.6.2). In the published

tr. I also tentatively took Agni as the referent of ─лm, but I now think that the ─лm in p─Бda a refers to the praiser in b, while the ─лm in c refers to the Aс╣Еgirases. (Remember that number is neutralized in ─лm.) The point is that the ┼Ы├║с╣гma- of the kindled fire accompanies each of these in order to allow the desired outcomes expressed in p─Бda b and d to occur – the singer to receive his reward and the Aс╣Еgirases to cause the cows to come out of the Vala cave. (I am tempted to tr. a version of тАЬmay the force be with you.тАЭ) So I would modify the tr. to тАЬWhen тАж the force тАж accompanies him [=singer], for the singer to take his reward; when it accompanies them [=Aс╣Еgirases] to the secret place [=Vala cave], тАж for (the cows) to go forth тАжтАЭ In d I take the three datives (pr├б) dhiy├й (pr├б) ├бyase m├бd─Бya not as triply parallel, but make the first and last further complements to ├бyase тАШto go forthтАЩ. The two pr├бтАЩs would in some sense structure these two parallel goal expressions: тАЬto go тЖРforth to insight>, тЖРforth to exhilaration>.тАЭ Needless to say, it is impossible to be certain about this interpr., but at least it hangs together.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As discussed in the published introduction, the next few vss. are very challenging; they have received multiple interpretations, which canтАЩt be discussed in detail here.

The vss. form a unity based on their shared vocab. (e.g., g├│he 6b, 7c, 8c; au┼Ыij├бsya 6b, 7c), their shared syntactic formulae (y├бd *─л 6a, y├бd ─лm 7a, 7c, and y├бd ─л 8d), and their shared metrical irregularity.

Griffith

Surely the power of Bharvara the mighty for ever helpeth to support the singer;
That which in Ausija’s abode lies hidden, to come forth for delight and for devotion.

Geldner

Wenn ihn ganz und gar die Wut des Bharavara-Stieres begleitet zum Sieg f├╝r den S├дnger, wenn er ihn heimlich im Versteck des Ausija - wenn er zum antreiben, zum Lauf, zur Kampflust geeignet ist.

Grassmann

Wenn nun der Drang des Stiers, der m├дchtig kauet, dem S├дnger hilft, um alles zu erlangen, Wenn du, verborgen im Versteck des Eifrers, hervor dann brichst zur Andacht und zur Freude;

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch as he has opened the doors of the cloud, and has supplied the rapid courses of the waters with (additional) torrents, so when the pious have recourse to Indra for food, he finds (it) in the haunt of the Gaura and Gavaya.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He finds it in the haunt of Gaura and Gavaya: vidat gaurasya gavayasya gohe: vidat here has no government;

Goha = gс╣Ыha, a dwelling; Gaura and Gavaya are two species of mс╣Ыga, deer or any wild animal; they are perhaps bos gavaus or gavaus frontalis and bibos gaurus or bos cavifrons; the purport of the phrase is that Indra obtains those two animals tau dvau pa┼Ыu labhate, either for himself as sacrificial flesh, or for his worshippers, some of whom, at least, even now, would not object to eat the flesh of the wild oxen

Jamison Brereton

When he opens out the mountainтАЩs enclosures into wide spaces and quickens the swift currents of the waters with gushes of milk,
he finds (the cows?) in the secret place of the buffalo, of the bull, when those of good insight convey him for the prize.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the play in the p─Бda-initial sequences: v├н y├бd (a), vid├бd (c), y├бd─л v(тАж) (d).

As noted in the published introduction, this last vs. of this obscure three-vs. group is the clearest indication of a Vala-myth subtext in the triad and thus serves as a species of poetic repair. As just noted ad vs. 7, the syntactic construction continues from vs. 7 and therefore indicates that the verses should be interpreted within the same conceptual framework. The vs. contains clear Vala vocabulary (esp. vid├бt) but leaves both subject and objects unexpressed, therefore allowing the double reading that I also suggested for vss. 6 and 7, namely that of the Vala myth and of the current ritual.

Although the reference is clearer in this vs., the grammar is another matter.

The major problem lies in the two parallel verbs vс╣Ыс╣Зv├й and jinv├й. Both appear to be 1st sg. middle presents to the stems 5th cl. vс╣Ыс╣З├│ti, vс╣Ыс╣Зut├й* and 1st cl. j├нnvati, -te respectively (so Grassmann, e.g.). However, Whitney and Macdonell group jinv├й instead with the marginally attested 5th cl. pres. (RV 1x jin├│с╣гi тАШbring to lifeтАЩ V.84.1), which would account better for the accent – and a 5th cl. pres. must of course ultimately underlie thematized j├нnvati (see Got┼Н, 1st Kl., 76). But 1st singulars do not fit the context at all, nor really do presents. Oldenberg tr. them both as 3rd sg. preterites (тАЬer тАж enth├╝llte тАж belebte тАжтАЭ) with, frustratingly, no comment. In this interpr. he seems to be following (or at least be in agreement with) S─Бyaс╣Зa., and the published translation reflects the same analysis, though with a historical present interpr. because of the apparent primary ending -├й. Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н take them as reflexive (Geldner) / passive (Witzel Got┼Н), with neut. pl.

subjects v├бr─Бс╣Гsi тАж j├бv─Бс╣Гsi (e.g., Geldner тАЬWenn sich die Breiten des Berges auftun,тАЭ etc.). Like Oldenberg, Geldner keeps silent about the grammar, but Witzel Got┼Н identify the two verbs as 3rd sg. statives construed with the neut. pl. as subject. I am torn. On the one hand, it is difficult to wring a standard 3rd sg. of the type I want from the forms in the text. On the other, I am very dubious about the existence of the тАЬstativeтАЭ – and even if this had been a separate grammatical category in the prehistory of Vedic, I doubt that it would have surfaced in just these two nonce forms in a single passage. Moreover, there is nothing semantically or functionally тАЬstativeтАЭ about either of these verbs, тАЬopen upтАЭ / тАЬquicken,тАЭ either in isolation or in this passage; note that even in the passive the Witzel Got┼Н tr. are overtly eventive: тАЬтАж aufgeschlossen werden тАж belebt werdenтАЭ (my italics). I also think that the mythic model found in the passage is against a reflexive or passive interpr. In the other standard depictions of the Vala myth, the opening of the mountain and the flowing out of cows/waters/dawns, are not events that happens spontaneously; the god Indra (/Bс╣Ыhaspati) or the Aс╣Еgirases cause these actions. The 3rd sg. vid├бt тАШhe foundтАЩ of 8c, a signature verb in the Vala myth, shows the typical pattern of expression in this myth. I therefore, uncomfortably, stand by the 3rd sg. transitive interpr. of these verbs, without being able to account for their form. They do belong to a little morphological pattern in 5th class presents, where 3rd sg. -├й is not uncommon: cf. ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зv├й, sunv├й, hinv├й. But unfortunately all three of the just cited forms are passive, and, in my reading, vс╣Ыс╣Зv├й and jinv├й are not. The neut. pl. v├бr─Бс╣Гsi in p─Бda a I take as a pun. The stem v├бras- definitely means тАШwide spaceтАЩ and is of course related to ur├║. However, as the object of тИЪvс╣Ы тАШencloseтАЩ (+ v├н = тАШunenclose, openтАЩ) and coming so soon after saс╣Гv├бraс╣Зeс╣гu (6d) тАШin the enclosuresтАЩ, it is not difficult to imagine that it could temporarily acquire a secondary association with тИЪvс╣Ы – hence my double tr. тАЬopens out the тАж enclosures into wide spaces.тАЭ I supply тАШcowsтАЩ as the first obj. of vid├бt on the basis of the use of this verb with obj. g─Б╠Бс╕е in the Vala myth elsewhere (e.g., I.62.3=X.68.1, II.19.3; note also the bovine vocab. gaur├бsya gavay├бya in the rest of the p─Бda), but in keeping with my double reading of this whole passage also supply тАШgoodsтАЩ as the desired discovery in the ritual context.

The sudhy├бс╕е тАШthose of good insightтАЩ are probably, with Witzel Got┼Н, the Aс╣Еgirases in the Vala myth, but I would add that this word would also identify the poets/priests at the ritual, in the double reading of this triad of verses that I favor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As discussed in the published introduction, the next few vss. are very challenging; they have received multiple interpretations, which canтАЩt be discussed in detail here.

The vss. form a unity based on their shared vocab. (e.g., g├│he 6b, 7c, 8c; au┼Ыij├бsya 6b, 7c), their shared syntactic formulae (y├бd *─л 6a, y├бd ─лm 7a, 7c, and y├бd ─л 8d), and their shared metrical irregularity.

Griffith

When he unbars the spaces of the mountains, and quickens with his floods the water-torrents,
He finds in lair the buffalo and wild-ox when the wise lead him on to vigorous exploit.

Geldner

Wenn sich die Breiten des Berges auftun und die Fluten der Gew├дsser sich regen in ihrem Na├Я, dann findet er in dem Versteck des Gaurab├╝ffels, des Gavayarindes, wenn die Frommgesinnten zu Gewinn ausfahren.

Grassmann

Wenn ich des Berges Weiten mir er├╢ffne, der Wasser Eile durch die Milch beschleun’ge, So find’ er im Versteck des br├╝nst’gen B├╝ffels, was ihm zur Labung zu die Frommen f├╝hren.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour auspicious hands, Indra, are the doers of good deeds; your two hands, Indra, are the extenders of wealth to him who praises you; what, Indra, is this delay? why do you not exhilarate us? why are you not delighted to make us gifts?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Auspicious are your hands and well-fashioned your palms, as ones that hold out largesse to the praiser, o Indra.
Why are you sitting it out? And why do you not find exhilaration? And why do you not rouse yourself higher and higher to give?

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is with considerable relief that we return to Indra.

In c I tr. k─Б╠Бte n├нс╣гattiс╕е – lit. тАЬWhat is this sitting down of yours?тАЭ – more idiomatically, to convey the exasperation of the singer.

The sequence k├нm u n├│ тАж, k├нс╣Г n├│d-ud u тАжis playful and, probably for that reason, somewhat difficult to parse. The n├│ in the first part of the phrase appears in the Pp. as no iti. Although normally a final -o of this type, generally found on the end of function words, represents -─Б/a plus the particle u (see Klein, Part. u, 168-78), Klein specifically lists this passage (168 n. 3) as a case where the presence of u is unlikely because тАЬthe syntactic environments within which u is found do not appear.тАЭ It is easy to see why he came to that judgment, esp. because thereтАЩs an u almost immediately preceding it and the 2nd u would come very late in the syntactic complex.

However, it is difficult to see what else to make of it, and the almost mirror image in the next p─Бda, where thereтАЩs a coalescence of n├б + ├║d into n├│d and an even later u following the complex of k├нm NEG PREV, suggests that the poet is having a bit of fun with u. Given the colloquial tone of this hemistich, we may also be seeing a looser deployment of particles and тАЬlittleтАЭ words characteristic of ordinary speech. (And who can resist the lilt of n├│d-ud u?) The multiplication of uтАЩs is completed by a form of the notorious -tav─Б╠Бu infinitive at the end of d.

Griffith

Auspicious are thy hands, thine arms wellfashioned which proffer bounty, Indra, to thy praiser.
What sloth is this? Why dost thou not rejoice thee? Why dost thou not delight thyself with giving?

Gl├╝ckbringend sind deine F├дuste und wohlgebildet deine H├дnde, die dem S├дnger die Ehrengabe ├╝berreichen, o Indra. Was soll dein Stillsitzen? Warum wirst du nicht lustig? Warum brennst du nicht darauf zu schenken?

Heilvoll, an Thaten reich sind deine H├дnde, wenn, Indra, sie dem S├дnger Gaben reichen; Wo rastest du? was eilst du nicht zum Rausche? hast du nicht Lust recht, Gaben uns zu schenken?

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThus (glorified), Indra, who is faithful (to his word), the lord of wealth, the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra, bestows rihes on man; so you, the praised of many, give us riches for our pious acts, that I may eat of your divine food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bestow riches on man: varivaс╕е p┼лrave kaс╕е = manuс╣гy─Бya dhanam karoti; or, it may be a reference to a descendant of Puru

Jamison Brereton

Just in this way, Indra, the real sovereign king of goods, the smiter of Vr╠еtra, made wide space for P┼лru.
O you praised by many, in accordance with your will, show your power over wealth for us. Might I have a share in your divine help.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This last vs. before the refrain shows some ring-composition with the beginning of the hymn: samr─Б╠Бс╣н (a) and kr├бtv─Б (c) respond to kr├бtuс╕е … samr─Б╠Бс╣н in 2c.

In p─Бda a saty├бс╕е тАШreal, really hereтАЩ may signal IndraтАЩs epiphany at the sacrifice.

Griffith

So Indra is the truthful Lord of treasure. Freedom he gave to man by slaying Vrtra.
Much-lauded! help us with thy power to riches: may I be sharer of thy Godlike favour.

English translation:

тАЬGlorified (in the past), glorified, Indra, at present, satisfy your worshipper with food, as rivers (are filled with water); lord of horses, a new hymn has been made for you; may we, possessed of chariots, be ever delighted in your praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАУ Now praised, o Indra, now being sung, make refreshment swell for the singer like rivers.
A new sacred formulation has been made for you, o you of the fallow bays. Through our insightful thought may we be charioteers who always win.

Now, Indra! lauded, glorified with praises, let power swell high, like rivers, for,the singer.
For thee a new hymn, Lord of Bays! is fashioned. May we, care-borne, through song be victqrs ever.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдиреБ) рд╕рджреНрдпрдГ (рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдиреБ) рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрднрдпрддреНрд░ рдЛрдЪрд┐ рддреБрдиреБрдШреЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреН (рдЗрд╖рдореН) (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╕рдХрд▓рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рдп (рдирджреНрдпрдГ) (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдкреАрдкреЗрдГ) рд╡рд░реНрдзрдп (рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐) (рддреЗ) рддреБрднреНрдпрдореН (рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдкреНрд░рд┐рдп (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдзрдирдореН (рдирд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдирд╡реАрдирдореН (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдпрд╛ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) рдмрд╣реБрд░рдерд╛рджреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рдГ) рд╕рд╕реЗрд╡рдХрд╛рдГ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдореИ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдВ рджрджреНрдпрд╛рддреН рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рддреЗрди рдпрдерд╛рд╡рддреН рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпреЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реерезрезрее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рдЬреНрдпрд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рджреЗрддреЛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдиреЗ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреА рдпрдерд╛рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реА. рее резрез рее
